Community rejects it under strict validation — nothing had ever booted it, since the security job only Trivy-*scans* the image) → removed; and **CI has no Neo4j service** (the plan's claim was false) → deferred to Session 16. **(5) §6.7 Neo4j telemetry:** disabled `client.allow_telemetry` + `dbms.usage_report.enabled`, the two default-on channels, **verified against `SHOW SETTINGS`** on the live 5.26 server rather than guessing the setting names (guessing wrong re-triggers the crash). **(6) Retro (4 changes, all approved):** sharpened **both** `/resume-session` (verify infra *runs* — boot the service / grep `ci.yml` — not just that config exists) **and** `/wrap-session` (don't *write* an unverified infra anchor into the handoff — the authoring-side fix, since both false claims were born there), after the handoff twice asserted false infra state this session; corrected the `backend/CLAUDE.md` `down_revision` pragma note (both revision lines can trip detect-secrets — pragma both); added a `backend/CLAUDE.md` note that a TDD integration test for a new module must import cleanly (or it breaks the fast-tier *collection*, not just the integration run). *Considered & rejected:* note-only on the infra-claim pattern (it recurred **twice this session** — clears the bar easily).
- **2026-06-08 — Session 14: backend SCA gate built + merged (PR #44); client DevSecOps notes folded; retro adds verify-at-build rule.** **(1) Scanner pinned by digest, not an Action (deviation from proposal D6, intent preserved):** `google/osv-scanner-action`'s root `action.yml` is a no-`runs:` metadata stub and its reusable workflows do a PR *diff* scan (misses an advisory already on `main`) or a SARIF-upload recursive scan — neither a scoped fail-on-any lockfile *step*. Built the gate as the **digest-pinned `ghcr.io/google/osv-scanner` container** (`scan source -L uv.lock --config=…`), which is *stronger* than the planned SHA-pin (a tag/digest can't move). D6's intent (pin the scanner immutably + soak it) held; the mechanism changed. *Considered & rejected:* the reusable workflow (wrong semantics/heavier), a hand-installed pinned binary (more YAML, weaker than a digest). **(2) Fail-on-any, scoped waivers in a sibling `infra/osv/`** (`osv-scanner.toml` enforced + `WAIVERS.md` register, condition-based expiry) — mirrors the Trivy split; no active waivers (green by *fixing* starlette, not suppressing). **(3) Client DevSecOps notes → `docs/PLAN_LONG.md`** new "Security & DevSecOps hardening — later" section: the *research-takes-precedence-over-feature-work* principle + two not-scheduled items (adopt Anthropic's `security-review` as a standing gate; an automated architecture-conformance CI check from the vault invariants). *Considered & rejected:* a self-hosted Gitea+runners CI (out of scope for a public GitHub portfolio; the client said skip it). **(4) Retro:** added a **verify-at-build** rule to `meta-architect:decompose-requirement` — a register decision resting on un-inspected external-tool behaviour (an Action's interface, a CLI's lockfile support, an API shape) is a *hypothesis* tagged `verify-at-build`, not settled, so a plan-first builder doesn't trust it blindly. *Considered & rejected:* note-only (the class recurred in spirit — both "SHA-pin the Action" and "parses uv.lock natively" needed build-time confirmation). *Worked well (no change):* my own `/review-pr` §2 grep sweep caught a stale acceptance-banner home my first reconciliation pass missed — the rule earned its keep.
- **2026-06-08 — Session 13: M2.S3 ExtractionAgent built + merged (PR #42); SCA decompose accepted; retro folds field-validator symmetry.** **(1) M2.S3 built test-first + merged (PR #42, green):** `ExtractionAgent` (first `LLMRouter` consumer) + `prompts/extraction.{pl,en}.j2` + `EntityCandidate`/`RelationCandidate`/`ExtractionProposal` schemas + the OQ-10 typed `ProviderResponseError` (both adapters raise on a malformed-`200` envelope; router records + fails over like a 5xx). Shared `extract_json` extracted to `agents/json_output.py`. **(2) Reviews — the layered gate earned its keep:** `/review-pr` (primary) caught typing/nits; **`/code-review` (the 2nd gate) caught a real bug `/review-pr` missed** — a `content: null` 200 envelope crashed the router with an uncaught `ValidationError` (no ledger row, no failover); folded as a null-content guard. Also folded: `_Router` protocol `weight` → `Literal` (would've broken M2.S4 wiring), **dropped the dead `prener_hints` param** (D3 intent minus the speculative surface), hardened `extract_json` for inline fences, blank `evidence_quote` → `None`. **(3) External review (post-merge) caught a gap both my passes missed:** blank `subject`/`predicate`/`object` validate as success (only `candidate_name` had a non-empty validator) → tracked cross-cutting (fix in M2.S4 or a quick PR). **(4) SCA decompose accepted** (`meta-architect:decompose-requirement`, triggered by a `starlette` 1.0.0 Dependabot alert CI didn't catch — Trivy scans only images, nothing scans `uv.lock`): owner approved the G1–G7 cluster — **osv-scanner**, **fail-on-any + scoped waivers**, SHA-pinned Action, reuse the Trivy waiver split (`infra/osv/`), `npm audit` left HIGH/CRITICAL, **§6.7 baseline control (no new INV)**, explicit `starlette==1.0.1` pin. `architecture/proposals/backend-dependency-advisory-scan.md` now `accepted`; **build deferred to next session (one branch); the spec §6.7 amendment lands *with* the build** (else it claims a gate CI doesn't run). Glossary +2 (`software-composition-analysis`, `defense-in-depth`). **(5) Retro:** folded **field-validator symmetry** into `/review-pr` §4 (when a schema validates one field for an invariant, audit every sibling field with the same semantic — the blank-relation gap slipped both my passes). *Considered & rejected:* note-only (the class is concrete + recurred this session — the null-content and blank-relation misses share the "degenerate-but-parseable passes as success" theme).
- **2026-06-08 — Session 12: M2.S3 design settled + spec §6.5 amended + review-model adapted + CVE wave-4 (PRs #39, #40).** A design/governance session, no production code. **(1) M2.S3 register resolved** (owner walked it after a by-hand `meta-architect:decompose-requirement` step 0 → accepted `architecture/proposals/m2s3-extraction-agent.md`): **per-paragraph** granularity (agent fragment-agnostic; spec §10 Q1 stays open); **single-paragraph agent**, resumable batch driver → M2.S4 (pause-and-ask propagates, never swallowed); **`candidate_name`** surface form, *not* `canonical_name` (D1 — canonical/PL-EN naming is M3); typed **`ProviderResponseError`** for malformed-`200` envelopes (D2/OQ-10 — failover-the-provider, distinct from schema-invalid→retry-the-prompt); **soft-flag `evidence_quote`** (drop quote, keep candidate — *rejected* hard-reject as punishing paraphrase); known-entities/custom-types as params now (Neo4j read wired M2.S4) / **PreNER hints deferred** (no speculative prompt complexity). **(2) Spec §6.5 router contract amended** (stop-and-amend): `route(self, task) -> LLMProvider` → `complete(messages, *, weight, task_type, json_schema=None) -> CompletionResult`; §6.5 + §11 "Failover" split envelope-malformed (→ failover) from schema-invalid (→ agent retry). Reconciled across README/plan/vault; ADR 0001 + M2.S2 history left intact. *Why:* the spec still described the pre-M2.S2 `route()` API the first router consumer would read. **(3) Review model adapted** (root `AGENTS.md` "Review model"): ChatGPT sub cancelled → Codex review is **secondary/best-effort, never block on it**; **`/review-pr` is the primary gate**; **`/code-review`** (multi-agent) added for substantive *code*; solo-review-blind-spot note for decision-state-flip PRs. *Considered & rejected:* ripping out all Codex references (over-reacting to a "we'll see"; §0 concurrent-agent rules kept as good hygiene pending confirmation). **(4) CVE-2026-42504 waived** (PR #40, wave 4 of Issue #22): Go-stdlib `mime.WordDecoder.DecodeHeader` DoS, compiled into pgvector-gosu + ollama; attribution verified vs NVD + pkg.go.dev/vuln/GO-2026-5038; reachability nil (127.0.0.1, trusted client); handled the pgvector→ollama sequential-unmask in one pass. **(5) Retro:** sharpened `/review-pr` §2 (same-PR proposal status-flip homes — INDEX row/next-steps + the plan task a decision changes) + the solo-review discipline note, after external review caught 3 §5b misses my self-review claimed clean. *Considered & rejected:* note-only/no-rule-change (the class recurred — #34 then #39 — so it earned the sharpening).
- **2026-06-02 — M2.S2 build: implementation-shape choices + the GPU-quota deferral (PR #36).** Confirmed while building the router/ledger (some with the owner mid-session, the rest folded from own-review + Codex on PR #36): **(1) The `LLMRouter` orchestrates `complete(weight, task_type)`** — agents call the router, not a provider; failover, the budget gate, and ledger recording have no other sensible home. (Rejected: the spec's literal `route()→LLMProvider`, which would scatter those cross-cutting concerns into every agent.) **(2) A `CostStore` Protocol** keeps the router unit-testable against an in-memory fake; the Postgres `llm_calls` impl is integration-tested separately. **(3) `PostgresCostStore` commits on its own short-lived connection per write** (not the request transaction) so a *failure* row survives a request that rolls back on that same failure — the §6.6 "explain why a batch stopped" trail must not vanish with the error it records. **(4) Provider 402 (out of credit) → `BudgetExceededError`** (same pause-and-ask type as our pre-dispatch cap); transport errors + 429/5xx fail over; 401 fails over but isn't quota; **only pure-429 cloud_free exhaustion → `QuotaExhaustedError`** (a bad key/outage/network failure surfaces the real error, not a false "quota spent" — Codex Risk fold-in). **(5) Schema/envelope-validation retry stays in the agent** (the ChunkingAgent pattern); the router owns transport + spend. The malformed-`200`-envelope record/failover gap is tracked as an M2.S3 cross-cutting follow-up. **(6) GPU-quota *remaining* deferred to M2.S5** (Codex Risk fold-in): `GET /llm/status` surfaces budget/spend/remaining-USD + GPU-seconds *consumed* + per-task breakdown now; the Ollama Cloud *remaining-quota* figure (spec §6.5/§6.6) needs their account API and lands with the M2.S5 panel — accepted deferral, consistent with ADR 0003's panel scope, marked in the endpoint docstring (no fabricated figure meanwhile). *Spec judged unchanged:* §6.5/§6.6 state the V1 goal "quota visible at all times"; this is sequencing its delivery, not contradicting it — so no spec amendment, only this recorded deferral.
- **2026-06-02 — Process (retro, Session 10): the decision-reconciliation discipline, encoded in three places.** The six-pass review saga on PR #34 was one recurring class — a *resolved decision left stale in another home* — and it cleared the retro bar easily (repeatable friction; it's also where my own `/review-pr` failed, rating the accepted-doc contradictions "banner covers it"). Three cross-referencing changes (all approved): **(1) `/review-pr` §2 — a "decision reconciliation" lens:** when a PR records/resolves a decision (flips a doc `proposed→accepted`, amends the spec, lands an ADR), verify by **exhaustive whole-repo grep, not the diff** — every home of the fact (spec's *other* sections, README, every `AGENTS.md`, plans, vault), the **tracking/registry/nav/status** notes that phrase it differently (ADR lists, priority queues, as-built snapshots, doc pointers), the **accepted artifact's whole body** (diagram/config/edge-cases, not just a banner), and **dated artifacts'** status; leave append-only history intact. Subsumes the Session-9-deferred vault lens (no-duplication + tense-honesty). **(2) Root `AGENTS.md` "Where knowledge lives" — the proactive authoring mirror:** reconcile a decision across every home in one pass, at authoring time, verified by sweep. **(3) Meta-architect `decompose-requirement` §5b — "reconcile the proposal to resolved state":** when the owner decides, bring the whole proposal (update-in-place) to resolved — register→Decided (incl. overrides), de-activate rejected options across diagram/config/edge-cases, strike the mirrored OQs, reconcile host-repo homes, grep-sweep. *Considered & rejected:* a standalone "resolve-a-decision" skill (a rule + the review check is enough — no new ritual earns its place); leaving it at `/review-pr` only (the authoring-side rule prevents the rework the review-side merely catches).
- **2026-06-02 — M2.S2 LLM-router decisions, settled via the meta-architect dogfood (ADR 0003; spec §6.5/§6.6 amended).** The architect's `review-architecture` + `decompose-requirement` passes (artefacts: `architecture/reports/2026-06-02-architecture-review.md`, `architecture/proposals/m2s2-llm-router-budget-cap.md`) framed the options; the owner resolved them. The cluster: **(1) Provider order = Ollama → OpenRouter → Grok → Anthropic → Google → OpenAI** — *not* Anthropic-first (overturns ADR 0001). OpenRouter leads the paid routes because one OpenAI-compatible endpoint reaches most vendor models. *Considered & rejected:* Anthropic/OpenAI-primary (ADR 0001's original). **(2) Hand-rolled `httpx` adapters, not vendor SDKs** (D2) — uniform shape, zero new deps, injectable-transport tests, visible swappability; cost = hand-written per-provider usage parsing. *Rejected:* 5 vendor SDKs (5 dependencies to vet/pin/soak, divergent shapes, buries the swappability). **(3) Build only `OllamaProvider` (extended) + `OpenRouterProvider` in M2.S2;** direct vendor adapters deferred to "as needed" (pulls OpenRouter forward from M2.S6). **(4) Control-first budget (G1):** on cloud_free-quota-exhaustion **or** daily-cap, the router **pauses and asks the user** — never silent paid escalation. Per-day USD hard cap, fail-closed (checked before dispatch). *Rejected:* auto-escalate-to-cheapest-paid-within-cap (owner chose control over unattended-batch convenience). **(5) `local_small` degrade target on a GPU-less host = cheapest cloud_free model** (resolves the live intra-spec contradiction §6.5 step-5-vs-hardware; OQ-3). **(6) INV-5 return-shape grows** — `CompletionResult`/Protocol carry usage; `OllamaProvider` stops discarding Ollama's `eval_count`/`prompt_eval_count` (OQ-7). One `llm_calls` table, nullable per tier (D4); tier/provider/model system-derived not caller-echoed (INV-7). **(7) Paid-egress consent gate deferred to M2.S5** (D5) — no sensitive data; documented at the egress point, not gated now (proposed temporary INV-9 dropped). **(8) Google/Gemini added** to the provider set. Recorded in **ADR 0003** (supersedes ADR 0001's provider-priority + quota-degradation consequences; three-tier model stands); spec §6.5/§6.6 amended; the architecture vault reconciled (OQ-3/6/7/8 struck, INV notes updated). *Process note:* this is the **first time the meta-architect produced design evidence that fed real product decisions** — treated as the dogfood evidence ADR 0002 §4 wants before any ritual-wiring (still deferred; the vault is now *navigable* from root `AGENTS.md` + `architecture/AGENTS.md`, which is awareness, not automation).
- **2026-06-02 — Session 9: meta-architect dogfood interlude — `architecture/` vault initialized + cross-agent hygiene (PRs #29/#30/#32, issue #31).** A cluster of linked decisions from the first live run of the plugin. **(1) The vault is committed** (not gitignored) — ADR 0002's default; it reads to an outsider as "we dogfooded our architect here," consistent with public-portfolio hygiene. *Considered & rejected:* gitignore (would hide the architecture work from the portfolio narrative). Landed as PR #30 (squash `bfbd37f`): `PROJECT` + `overview` (nine-layer system seed, grounded in the as-built present), `invariants` (8 named, INV-8 flagged temporary), `open-questions` (operator's review-then-strategize queue + 5 seed-pass gaps + a *reference* to spec §10), a 14-term cross-linked `glossary/`, plus `learning-log`/`CHANGELOG`/`INDEX` and empty dirs for later runs. **(2) The vault references, never copies, the spec/plans/code** — this was the run's core stress-test, and **two Codex review passes** sharpened it: no-duplication (the `overview` Data layer had restated the §6.4 schema, `cascade-matching` the §3.3 algorithm → both trimmed to the architectural *reading* + a §-reference) and tense-honesty (`PROJECT` Identity + `invariants` INV-2 described unbuilt extraction/router/consent features in present tense → reframed as-built-vs-planned, matching INV-1). My own `/review-pr` + a same-session fold of a "Built in M2.S2" overclaim came first; Codex's passes caught the rest. **(3) Codex = PR-review only; the boundary is documented both ways.** Codex runs on host-Windows over a UNC view of this WSL checkout (no WSL shell), so it reviews but does not edit Story Forge code; its own runtime notes (`.codex/RUNTIME_NOTES.md` + `AGENTS.md` §0) landed as PR #32 when they surfaced uncommitted in the shared tree — kept out of the vault PR to stay surgical. **(4) Concurrent-agent shared-tree rule** added to root `AGENTS.md` §0 (retro outcome): stage explicit paths (never `git add -A`); surface foreign uncommitted changes, never absorb or delete them. **(5) Deferred:** wiring the meta-architect skills into the rituals (ADR 0002) — now explicitly carrying the vault-review lens for `/review-pr` and **issue #31** (slug/filename carve-out for the uppercase notes). *Considered & rejected:* encoding the vault-review lens into `/review-pr` now (one data point; honors ADR 0002's integrate-after-living-with-it).
- **2026-06-02 — meta-architect plugin incubated in-repo + `AGENTS.md` made canonical + self-improving Codex review (PR #27, squash `f3fdeef`).** A cluster of decisions. **(1) Incubate the architect as in-repo dev tooling.** A domain-agnostic product architect — an agent persona + three skills (`initialize-project-architecture`, `decompose-requirement`, `review-architecture`) producing only Markdown design artefacts into an Obsidian vault, teaching architecture vocabulary, never writing production code. It is **dev tooling, not a product feature** → deliberately *not* in `story-forge-poc-spec.md`; lives as a self-contained `meta-architect/` directory so extraction later = moving the folder. Wired via committed `.claude/settings.json` (`extraKnownMarketplaces` relative `./meta-architect` + `enabledPlugins`). Rationale + sequencing in **`docs/decisions/0002`**. *Considered & rejected:* standalone repo from day one (couldn't dogfood while building); global `~/.claude` install (not reproducible); scattering skills into `.claude/skills/` (muddies extraction); hard-wiring the workflow integration now (premature — validate after the first run). **(2) The plugin's own framework, as its own MADR ADRs:** nine analysis layers with **Compliance/Audit split out of Security** (`meta-architect/decisions/0001`), a **glossary-as-knowledge-graph** (one note per term, not one file — `0002`), and a three-mode **vault update model** (regenerated / append-only / update-in-place) dropping a misleading `frozen` status (`0003`). **(3) `AGENTS.md` is canonical** in every directory; each `CLAUDE.md` is a **symlink** to it — one source of truth, read by Codex (`AGENTS.md`) and Claude (`CLAUDE.md`) alike — gratuitous tool-naming neutralized (factual infra like `.claude/settings.json` / `${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}` kept). Dev env is Linux/WSL/macOS (symlink-aware; noted in `AGENTS.md`). **(4) A self-improving Codex review skill** (`.agents/skills/review-pr/`) that reads/appends its own `lessons.md`; Claude's `/review-pr` learned to filter Codex's Windows/UNC cross-environment artifacts (false-positive filemode/symlink diffs). **Reviewed** via `/review-pr` (own) + Codex — converged on the vault-only Bash guardrail; folded that + a stale `proposals/<slug>/decisions.md` path; the filemode "change" was a Codex Windows/UNC artifact (no fix needed — canonical `git ls-files -s` = `100755`). **Sequencing:** build now (this PR); first live `initialize` run next session; integrate into the rituals only after learning from it.
- **2026-06-01 — Process (retro): cwd-robust gate invocation + "a retro is a reflective pass".** Two fixes from this session's retrospective (which itself was nearly skipped — the user had to prompt for it twice, which is *why* the second fix exists). **(1) cwd foot-gun killed at the source.** Running `python3 scripts/check_dependency_age.py` from `backend/` fails with "No such file" (the script lives at repo root); it bit 3× this session and once in Session 3, where we wrongly dismissed it as "the from-repo-root note already guards it." The note didn't — recurrence proved it. `/add-dependency` and `/wrap-session` now invoke it cwd-independently as `python3 "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/scripts/check_dependency_age.py"`, verified working from `backend/`. The script was already cwd-independent (`Path(__file__)`); the bug was always the *invocation path*, so this corrects the Session-3 misdiagnosis rather than touching the script. **(2) `/wrap-session` step 2 clarified:** a retro is a *reflective pass* (what ran, what recurred, what helped), not merely folding an explicit user directive — conflating the two is how the cwd gotcha survived a session. *Considered & rejected:* hardening the script itself (already cwd-independent); a Makefile/task-runner for all gates (over-engineering for one script).
- **2026-06-01 — M2.S1 PreNERAgent + the §6.7 direct-URL-wheel channel + doc-over-memory rule (PR #25 feature, this PR governance).** Several linked decisions. **(1) GitHub-release wheels as a new §6.7 dependency channel.** spaCy's pretrained models (`pl_core_news_lg`, `en_core_web_lg`) aren't on PyPI — only versioned wheels on GitHub Releases. Rather than relax the baseline, ran the security-baseline-amendable flow: spec §6.7 gained a "Direct-URL wheel channel" clause (PEP 508 `name @ url`, exact-by-construction, SHA-256-locked in `uv.lock`), `check_dependency_age.py` learned to gate these on the GitHub **asset** upload date, `/add-dependency` documents the procedure. OSV is the one genuinely-N/A rule (artifacts not indexed); residual risk bounded by official publisher + locked hash + weights-only payload. *Considered & rejected:* `spacy download` (unpinned runtime fetch); a manual WAIVERS-style hole (the gate enforces it automatically instead). **(2) Asset date, not tag date (Codex P2).** A wheel can be added to/replaced on an older release after its tag was cut; since uv locks the new bytes, the tag's `published_at` would let a fresh artifact pass the soak. Gate reads the matching asset's `updated_at`. The model assets date 2024-09-29 vs the tag's 2024-09-30 — proof the two differ. **(3) Models in an optional `models` dependency group.** The wheels are ~950 MB; default `uv sync` (and CI) skips them, the model-loading tests auto-skip via `importlib.find_spec`, and the pure `candidates_from_entities`/`map_spacy_label` seam keeps `extract()`'s logic CI-tested without them (own-review #1). `spacy` itself stays a core dep (needed for mypy). `uv sync --group models` locally. **(4) Layering carve-out.** spaCy is imported directly in `agents/prener_agent.py` (not behind a Protocol) — documented exception in `src/story_forge/CLAUDE.md` for deterministic local NLP; revisit a `NerPipeline` Protocol only when a second NER backend appears (e.g. the finetuned model below). **(5) PreNER is recall-first, deliberately imperfect.** It surfaces candidates; the LLM ExtractionAgent (M2.S3) + §3.3 Stage-4 human review correct types, and the accumulated corrections are the training data for a **custom finetuned spaCy model** later (recorded in `PLAN_LONG`). So tests assert the agent's contract, not model accuracy — encoded in `backend/CLAUDE.md`. **(6) Process: document in the repo, not agent memory.** Durable knowledge (decisions, conventions, follow-ups) goes into the spec/plan/`CLAUDE.md`/skills — the file the next contributor consults — never only in private agent memory. Encoded in root `CLAUDE.md` + `/retro` + `/wrap-session`; the three memories this session accrued were migrated here and into those files, then cleared. *Also recorded:* web research runs in the **main loop**, since background subagents can't surface permission prompts and get web/shell tools auto-denied (root `CLAUDE.md` session guidance). **Reviewed** via `/review-pr` (own) + Codex; both folded — CI-coverage seam (#1), GitHub-token/403 gate robustness (#3), layering note (#2), asset-date gating (Codex P2). CI green across all four jobs; squash-merged `e80ef94`.
- **2026-05-27 — Wave-3 CVE response + post-PR-23 waiver audit + /review-pr §5/§8 amendments.** Four linked actions, all chained from one Codex catch. **(1) Wave-3 CVE response (PR #23, squash `0057044`).** Three new HIGH gosu Go-stdlib CVEs (CVE-2026-39823 `html/template` `<meta>` XSS; CVE-2026-39825 `net/http/httputil` ReverseProxy; CVE-2026-39826 `html/template` `<script>` XSS) hit pgvector and ollama together via the sequential-Trivy unmask pattern; waived per-image with reachability rationales. Tripped the WAIVERS.md "build our own image if this happens a third time" threshold (recorded 2026-05-26 after wave 2). Evaluation tracked in [Issue #22](https://github.com/yaaisiu/story-forge/issues/22), pgvector-scoped — gosu is shipped by the *postgres* image, not by pgvector, so the recipe only escapes the treadmill if `postgres:17-trixie` rebuilds faster than pgvector does (that's the issue's load-bearing first task). **(2) Codex P2 fold.** Initial CVE-2026-39823 rationale named `net/url`; Codex caught that the CVE is actually in `html/template` (verified against pkg.go.dev/vuln GO-2026-4982 + NVD). Outcome unchanged (gosu doesn't render templates) but the *justification* needed to match the real code path. My own `/review-pr` missed it. **(3) Existing-waiver audit (user-requested, this wrap commit).** Verified 39 pre-PR-23 CVE rationales against NVD: **39/39 package attributions correct** — Codex's catch was isolated, not a repo-wide pattern. Five minor description tightenings folded (none changing reachability): CVE-2025-61723 "std" → "encoding/pem"; CVE-2026-25679 IPv6-specific → general host/authority validation; CVE-2026-33811 DoS → double-free + crash severity; CVE-2026-29111 dropped over-claimed "arbitrary code execution" (actual is DoS per NVD); CVE-2026-40356 "integer overflow" → "integer underflow". Running the audit *while the Codex catch was fresh* gave empirical confidence the bug-class was an isolated incident. **(4) Process amendments from retro** (both approved). `/review-pr` §5 gains: *"verify each CVE's package attribution against an authoritative source (pkg.go.dev/vuln / NVD); Trivy's title text can reference a different CVE and silently mislead"* — memorable example: CVE-2026-39823's title began with "CVE-2026-27142 fixed a vulnerability in which URLs were not correctly...". `/review-pr` §8 gains: *"sequential-Trivy unmask — don't declare ready-to-merge on first green scan when a PR changes a Trivy waiver or image pin"* — pattern is 3-for-3 (#2, #4, #23). `/pin-image` already encodes the scan-all-images-up-front check for new pins; `/review-pr` §8 carries the equivalent for waiver-only PRs. **Considered + rejected:** a new `/verify-waiver` skill (insufficient recurrence — fresh waivers ~3× per year; the check belongs as a bullet in `/review-pr`); a separate "Last audited" field in WAIVERS.md (redundant with "Last reviewed", which is now 2026-05-27); an ADR for the wave-3 escalation (the durable record — WAIVERS.md preamble + Issue #22 + PR #23 squash body — already serves).
- **2026-05-27 — M2 sliced into 6 resumable sessions + §3.3 drift corrected.** Three linked decisions. **(1) Slice shape:** S1 PreNERAgent (spaCy, deterministic) → S2 paid LLM adapters (~~Anthropic-first~~ → OpenRouter-first, overturned 2026-06-02 — ADR 0003) + `LLMRouter` + budget tracking → S3 ExtractionAgent → S4 Neo4jAdapter writes (no dedupe) → S5 frontend graph viewer (cytoscape) + agent activity panel (§8.5) → S6 OpenRouterProvider + polish. Order follows spec §7's pipeline order (Pre-NER step 3 before LLM extraction step 4), so dependency is the slice rule, not a reordering. **(2) M2.S1 = PreNERAgent (deterministic) over "router first".** Considered & rejected: opening with paid-adapter + router (the alternative the Session 6 wrap-handoff floated). Router-first would couple three decisions in one session (which paid provider, where the budget knob lives, router shape) and ship no extraction; PreNER-first is standalone, deterministic, follows the project preference for deterministic methods over LLM where they suffice, and gives ExtractionAgent (S3) a real input set before it's designed. Also considered: read the spec sections first and decide afterward — the right move and the one we took, which confirmed §7 step 3 places Pre-NER ahead of step 4 LLM extraction. **(3) §3.3 cascade-matching drift in the M1→M2 handoff: corrected.** The Session 6 wrap-handoff parenthetically scoped "§3.3 Stages 1+2+3 as M2 scope; Stage 4 review queue is M3" — but spec §9 M2 says literally "Save entities to Neo4j without cascade (everything = new entity for now)" and §9 M3 lists MatchingAgent (Stages 1+2), JudgeAgent (Stage 3), **and** the review queue (Stage 4) all together. Per the workflow rule, spec wins. The slice now matches: M2 has *no* cascade work at all; every extracted candidate becomes a fresh Neo4j node. Spec is unchanged (it was already right); only the plan was sloppy. This is the kind of drift `/resume-session` exists to catch — flagging it here as a process win, not just a fix.
- **2026-05-26 — Session 6: five linked decisions (frontend upload + outline UI, M1 close).** (1) **shadcn install path: B-now / A-when-needed.** Plain Tailwind alone for Session 6; hand-vendor primitives at first real need, documented in `frontend/src/components/ui/CLAUDE.md` at first use. Chose over the official CLI macro because the CLI bulk-installs deps without going through `/add-dependency`'s §6.7 discipline and writes files into the repo opaquely. The minimal `cn()` helper at `src/lib/utils.ts` matches shadcn's canonical location so first-vendored primitives can import it unmodified. (2) **Outline editor scope: Option B (raw_text override + persist on the existing structure endpoint).** Considered & rejected: read-only editor (would miss the "outline editable in UI" milestone goal); full delete-and-replace + PATCH (overshoots one conversation). Manual mode is deterministic so local-preview ↔ backend-parse drift risk is low; auto/hybrid edit-preview still deferred (needs an LLM dry-run path). Spec §7 step 1/2 amended to record the response/body shape. (3) **Defense-in-depth empty-`raw_text` guard, two layers.** My `/review-pr` Should-fix #1 (UI disables submit when manual/hybrid textarea is empty + inline hint) and Codex's P1 (hook drops the override when raw_text is empty/whitespace) caught the *same* destructive-overwrite bug with *different* fix mechanisms. Folded both — the UI guard prevents the click, the hook guard catches anything that bypasses the UI (programmatic caller, future regression). (4) **CORS allowlist also accepts `http://127.0.0.1:5173` and `http://127.0.0.1:3000`** (§6.7 spec amended with rationale, root `CLAUDE.md` updated, `config.py` default + `.env.example` extended). Real-browser smoke test caught that Vite binds to `127.0.0.1` by default but the original allowlist only named `localhost` — uploads succeeded backend-side but the browser rejected the response. Same loopback socket, same trust boundary; both name forms point at it. Kills the class rather than the instance — the cross-cutting CORS follow-up is removed. (5) **Planning docs reorganized.** `PLAN_SHORT.md` / `PLAN_LONG.md` moved into `docs/`; new `docs/CLAUDE.md` documents the handoff-block contract, the Decided/Blocked/Done structure, and the cross-cutting curation rule (carried by hand at each milestone roll — nothing moves automatically). Path references in root `CLAUDE.md`, `/resume-session`, `/wrap-session`, and README reconciled.
- **2026-05-26 — Process (retro): three rule additions from Session 6.** (1) **`/review-pr` §8 amendment**: "same bug, different fixes — consider folding both." When `/review-pr` and Codex flag the same bug class with different suggested mechanisms (UI guard vs hook guard, in our case), the default isn't "pick one and dedup the other" — it's *consider folding both as defense-in-depth*, especially for destructive bugs (data loss, silent overwrite). Two independent reviewers converging on a class while diverging on mechanism is the signal the bug deserves belt-and-suspenders. Example: empty-`raw_text` overwrite — both folds landed (PR #18). (2) **`backend/CLAUDE.md` "Running locally" note**: before first run against the dev backend, `uv run alembic upgrade head` from `backend/`. Tests use a throwaway DB so this gap was invisible until the verify-skill smoke walk 500'd on `relation "projects" does not exist`. Idempotent; safe to re-run. (3) **§6.7 CORS amendment** (described in Decided above) — recorded here as a process change because it removes the cross-cutting follow-up and makes both `localhost` / `127.0.0.1` first-class loopback origins for dev. **Considered + rejected:** a `/pin-image` amendment about "if it bit you once, expect the next CVE wave in days not weeks" (the WAIVERS.md preamble we wrote *this session* already records the empirical pattern + the "build our own image at occurrence 3" threshold — a `/pin-image` line on top would be ceremony); a `/verify` shadow about "handoff to user for GUI surface" (one-off in this no-Chromium env, working around the skill's PASS/FAIL/BLOCKED/SKIP vocabulary by saying "PASS (backend) | HANDOFF (GUI)" was fine and didn't cost real time); a "cross-layer scope expansion" rule (AskUserQuestion handled it; no recurring friction to encode).
- **2026-05-26 — Session 6: pgvector CVE-rot recurrence threshold recorded.** The pgvector image (`pgvector/pgvector:0.8.2-pg17-trixie`) was hit by a *second* CVE-staleness wave in 5 days against the same 2026-05-15 rebuild (Issue #4 → PR #19). Resolved by extending `infra/trivy/pgvector.trivyignore` with 11 new HIGHs (1 krb5 OS + 10 Go-stdlib in `gosu`), all reachability-justified. A pattern note in `infra/trivy/WAIVERS.md` calls out the recurrence explicitly: if this happens a *third* time, strongly consider building our own image (`postgres:17-trixie` + `apt-get install postgresql-17-pgvector`) so we own the rebuild cadence. Documented so a reader knows we're aware of the treadmill, not surprised by it.
- **2026-05-25 — Session 5: six linked decisions (frontend shell + typed client).** (1) **shadcn/ui deferred to Session 6** — Session 5's failing test is "app shell renders under router + query provider", which doesn't need any shadcn primitive. Installed Tailwind alone; primitives land when the upload/outline UI actually consumes them. Smaller, more honest diff for the shell session. (2) **M0 `/health` page removed, not converted.** It was M0 connectivity scaffolding, not a feature. Converting it to a TanStack Query hook would have invented a feature we don't need (Karpathy "no speculative features") — Session 6's upload screen replaces this view anyway. (3) **`openapi.json` captured to a file committed in the repo** (`frontend/openapi.json`), regenerated via `backend/scripts/dump_openapi.py`. Keeps the frontend build hermetic (no live-backend dependency in CI / for frontend-only contributors) and surfaces backend schema drift as a visible PR diff. (4) **`openapi-typescript@7.13.0` runs via `npx`, not installed.** Upstream peer is `typescript@^5.x` while the project is on `typescript@6.0.3`; `npx -y openapi-typescript@7.13.0` (pinned in the `generate:api` npm script) sidesteps the `ERESOLVE` cleanly without project-wide `--legacy-peer-deps`. Trade-off acknowledged: not visible to `scripts/check_dependency_age.py` / `npm audit`; pin-time age + OSV verified manually and documented in `frontend/src/lib/api/CLAUDE.md`. Revisit when upstream supports TS 6. (5) **Shared `ErrorResponse(BaseModel)` + `responses={...}` on both `/stories` routes** (folded from Codex P2). Every `HTTPException` the routes raise (400/404/409/413/415/502) now appears in OpenAPI typed as `ErrorResponse`, so Session 6's hooks can discriminate failure modes by status code with proper types. 422 is deliberately left undeclared to preserve FastAPI's auto-generated `HTTPValidationError` shape; the overload (`ChunkingTooLongError` also raises 422 with a `{detail: str}` body) is tracked as a cross-cutting follow-up. (6) **Vitest wired into the frontend CI job** (`.github/workflows/ci.yml` `- name: Vitest`). The shell render test existed in the first commit but no CI step invoked it; folded from own-review (B1). A test that runs only locally is half a test.
- **2026-05-25 — Session 5: QuerySentinel makes test wrappers load-bearing.** The shell test originally mounted `<QueryClientProvider>` around an `<AppShell>` that has no TanStack Query usage — the wrapper was decorative, and the test docstring's claim ("proves both providers are wired correctly") was a lie. Folded via a tiny in-test `<QuerySentinel />` that calls `useQueryClient()` (throws without a provider). Verified by removing the provider in the test and confirming the test fails with the missing-provider error. The provider chain is now defended from Session 5, not from "whenever Session 6 happens to add a real hook."
- **2026-05-25 — Process (retro): three rule additions from Session 5.** (1) Added a **`/review-pr` §4 bullet**: "FastAPI routes declare every non-2xx outcome they raise in `responses={...}`" — Codex caught the gap on `/stories/{id}/structure`; my own `/review-pr` missed it. Also documents the 422 trap (declaring 422 clobbers FastAPI's validation typing). (2) Added a **`/review-pr` §6 bullet**: "Render-test wrappers must be load-bearing" — every provider / context / fixture wrapping a render test must be exercised by the asserted-on subtree or by an explicit sentinel component. (3) Added a **`/review-pr` §6 bullet**: "A new test runner / category / glob is wired into CI before merge" — the test-driven rule is structurally bypassed if CI doesn't execute the test. (4) Mirrored the FastAPI rule as an **authoring** rule in `backend/src/story_forge/CLAUDE.md` (new `## API routes` section). The review and authoring sides now both name the rule, so it's caught both when written and when reviewed. **Considered + rejected:** a rule about "grep for existing CI steps before adding a duplicate plan item" (near-miss with `npm audit`; due diligence caught it on its own — not skill-worthy); a "what to do when a peer-dep conflict makes the pin unworkable" branch in `/add-dependency` (edge case enough that adding it would be over-engineering until we hit it twice).
- **2026-05-25 — Chunking default lowered: `gpt-oss:120b-cloud` → `gpt-oss:20b-cloud`.** Verified against Ollama's current cloud catalog (the `:20b-cloud` tag is confirmed available, same gpt-oss family, "Low Usage" tier vs the 120b's "Medium Usage" — lighter quota, same Ollama API, same JSON structured-output behavior). Rationale: **chunking is a structural JSON task** (find `##`/`###` boundaries, return paragraph ranges with one-sentence summaries), not deep Polish prose generation; a 6× smaller model in the same family is sufficient and meaningfully cheaper to run. Spec §6.5 / §5 hardware tier / §9 example references softened to cite the new default ("`gpt-oss:20b-cloud` for chunking, larger variants for heavier tasks"); not a tier change (still cloud_free). Bump back to 120b / try `qwen3.5:cloud` if proposal quality is short on real long-form PL text — kept the option open in the .env.example comment. Considered + rejected: `qwen3.5:cloud` (better PL breadth — 201 languages — but Medium-Usage tier with no quota savings, multimodal weight we don't need; the right default for *later* prose-quality work, not chunking).
- **2026-05-25 — Process (retro): two `/review-pr` amendments from Session 4.** (1) Added a "dispatch-level confusion in nested structures" bullet to `/review-pr` §1: when code branches on a property at one level of a tree, check the invariant isn't at a neighboring level. Codex caught the hybrid bug — `_fill_untitled` dispatched on chapter-untitled and silently discarded an explicitly-titled scene that lived *inside* an implicit chapter (`### Cold Open` before any `##`). My own `/review-pr` ran after the fold and didn't list this class. (2) Clarified `/review-pr` §3 Simplicity bullet: an abstraction that net-removes existing debt (type-ignores, repeated boilerplate, branches) is a refactor, not speculation; simplicity argues *for* it. Example: the `OutlineProposer` `Protocol` introduced in the same PR removed 11 `# type: ignore[arg-type]` markers. **Considered + rejected:** a rule encoding AskUserQuestion cadence (the tool description already says reserve it for genuine forks — I asked once for a conventional default, self-discipline observation only); a rule forcing `/review-pr` *before* Codex's review (hard to encode without implementation friction, surfaced as awareness).
- **2026-05-25 — Session 4: five linked decisions (chunking modes + persistence).** (1) **Markers are heading *levels*, not literal "Chapter"/"Scene" words** — `##` opens a chapter and the trailing text is the title (`## The Crossing`, not the word "Chapter"); `#` is the story title and is not a structural boundary; `###` opens a scene. Plan wording clarification, not a spec change (§3.1 already showed `##`/`###` as the marker shape; the literal title was just an example). (2) **Hybrid fills only untitled *scenes* (per-scene dispatch).** First pass dispatched per-chapter and lost explicit scene anchors inside implicit chapters (Codex P1 catch); the corrected rule preserves every explicit `##`/`###` verbatim. (3) **Windowing: guard now, window-and-stitch later.** `auto`/`hybrid`-fill LLM paths raise `ChunkingTooLongError` above `max_input_words` (a constructor knob, not a new env setting); manual mode handles any size. The proper pre-split + per-window + stitch sub-system is a tracked cross-cutting follow-up — premature to build before auto is actually run on a 50k-word input. (4) **Endpoint = one-shot build+persist; re-structure returns 409.** `POST /stories/{id}/structure?mode=...` reads the story's stored raw text and persists the tree in a single call. The accept/edit loop (§7 step 2 "user accepts/edits before save") is a frontend interaction — deferred to Session 6 where the editor exists. 409 over silent-append on a second run; delete-and-replace is a frontend-driven follow-up. (5) **Outline carries `summary`.** The agent produces summaries and the DB columns already exist; dropping them would be lossy. Manual mode leaves them `None`, which is correct.
- **2026-05-25 — Session 4: DB write lock is taken *after* the LLM build, not before.** The structure route's `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE` originally wrapped the whole handler — including the seconds-long LLM call. Folded into the same PR after `/review-pr`: build the outline first (no DB state needed beyond the story.raw_text we already read), then take the lock for the small writes window, re-check `list_chapters` under the lock, then insert. The 409 race is still closed (concurrent POSTs serialize on the lock; the second sees the persisted tree). Honest trade: a true contention test needs parallel connections, which the txn-sharing `db_conn` fixture doesn't fit — defense-in-depth verified by reading.
- **2026-05-22 — Process (retro): created `/review-pr` skill, wired into CLAUDE.md Merge flow (Session 3).** A Story Forge PR-review skill that does a correctness/bug-finding pass *plus* the project lens (spec/plan fidelity, layering, §6.7 gaps CI can't catch, test discipline, hygiene, merge-readiness); report-only, complements Codex (PR #11, `d90ed76`). Hardened mid-session after Codex caught two things its first version missed — added an *output-schema strength* check (malformed-but-parseable must fail, not pass as success) and a *prompt-injection safety* check (never recover prompt structure by reparsing output rendered with untrusted content). Referenced from CLAUDE.md's Merge flow as the explicit "your own review" step. Considered + rejected: hardening `check_dependency_age.py` for cwd-independence — on inspection it already uses `Path(__file__)` and is cwd-independent; the failures were invocation errors (running `python3 scripts/…` from `backend/`), which the "from repo root" note already guards.
- **2026-05-22 — Chunking refocus + cloud_free default (Session 3).** Two linked decisions. (1) **GPU-less dev host** → the local_small tier is impractical (CPU-only 9B too slow for interactive use), so chunking defaults to **cloud_free** (Ollama Cloud); local_small stays a config swap for a GPU-backed host. Because both tiers speak the Ollama API, this is a host/key flip in `OllamaProvider`, not a code-path change. Spec §6.5 (hardware para + agent table) and §7 step 2 amended with rationale. (2) **LLM chunking is not the primary path.** §3.1 already defines three modes; manual (`## Chapter`/`### Scene` markers) + hybrid are deterministic, free, and more reliable than a small model on *marked* text — and paragraphs are already deterministic (`domain/parsing.py`). So `ChunkingAgent` is reframed as the auto/**fallback** path for *unmarked* text + the canonical first agent demonstrating the agent pattern (prompt + Pydantic schema + retry); the deterministic manual/hybrid chunker (Session 4) is the everyday primary path. Session order unchanged (3 = LLM auto, 4 = manual/hybrid + persistence). The `CHUNKING_LOCAL_MAX_WORDS=4000` threshold is kept as a config knob (conservative; meaningful only when a local tier is configured), not a hardcoded magic number. **Tests stay mocked** — the smallest Ollama Cloud model is the runtime default and fine for manual smoke checks, but agent unit tests use a mocked `LLMProvider` per `backend/src/story_forge/CLAUDE.md`.
- **2026-05-21 — Language detection: `langdetect==1.0.9` (Session 2).** Over `fasttext`: `langdetect` is pure-Python and ships its own profiles (no `lid.176` model artifact to download out-of-band — pinnable, offline-friendly, no extra supply-chain surface), and PL/EN is an easy discrimination on 5k–50k-word prose where fasttext's short-text accuracy edge doesn't apply. Seeded (`DetectorFactory.seed = 0`) for deterministic output.
- **2026-05-21 — Upload creates a new `Project` per file (Session 2).** A `Story` needs a `project_id` and there is no project-selection UI/endpoint yet, so the upload route creates a `Project` (name = filename stem, language = detected) alongside the `Story`. The detected language lives on `Project` (the `Story` model has no language field). Revisit when project management lands.
- **2026-05-21 — Sandboxed uploads stored without a DB path column (Session 2).** Original bytes are written to a dedicated dir (UUID-named, `0o700` dir / `0o600` file, no exec — spec §6.7), and the parsed text is stored in `Story.raw_text`; the saved path is *not* tracked in Postgres. Satisfies §6.7 with no spec/migration change. The dir chmod is explicit (not `mkdir(mode=…)`, which is umask-masked and ignored for an existing dir).
- **2026-05-21 — Per-request DB connection, no pool (Session 2).** `adapters/db.py` `get_connection` opens one `AsyncConnection` per request (commit on success / rollback on error). A pool (`psycopg_pool`) is deferred as speculative for a single-user local app. `libpq_kwargs` preserves URL query options (`sslmode`, timeouts) so a managed-Postgres URL still works (Codex P1); `conftest` reuses the same helper.
- **2026-05-21 — Process (retro): PR-first / `/wrap-session`-last, encoded in the wrap skill.** The session-close order is commit → PR → CI + Codex review → fold fixes → squash-merge → *then* `/wrap-session` (which lands the separate `docs: close Session N` commit). Added a preflight step 0 to `wrap-session` and reframed its step 8 (commit the wrap's *own* bookkeeping, not the feature). Also added a `backend/CLAUDE.md` test convention: bind credential-like values to a variable so `detect-secrets` doesn't flag them (prefer over baseline/pragma edits).
- **2026-05-21 — Issue #4 resolved: pgvector → `0.8.2-pg17-trixie`, ollama → `0.24.0`, both scoped-waivered (PR #6, `4cb92a2`).** pgvector pinned at 6 days old (the pre-approved §6.7 bend); trixie is the cleanest base pgvector ships (9 OS CVEs vs bookworm 13; older 0.8.1-trixie = 42; no UBI variant). Fixing pgvector unmasked a second stale image — ollama `0.22.1` (sequential Trivy masking, same as neo4j→pgvector in #2). ollama bumped to `0.24.0` (freshest aged stable, 7 days, no bend), which dropped the CRITICAL + 6 others (17 → 12 HIGH, 0 CRIT). Residual CVEs no tag can fix are waived per-CVE: pgvector's OS CVEs (no fresher rebuild exists) + bundled `gosu`/Go-stdlib; ollama's compiled-in Go-stdlib + `buger/jsonparser` — all assessed not network-reachable on a 127.0.0.1 single-user deployment (gnutls unused; mostly DoS; cert-validation needs MITM). Added **`infra/trivy/WAIVERS.md`**, a consolidated review register of every waived CVE across images (fixed-in versions + drop conditions), backreferenced from each scoped `.trivyignore`; waivers stay per-image, never repo-wide.
- **2026-05-21 — Process (retro): amended `/pin-image` with three lessons from Issue #4.** (1) When a local Trivy scan can't be read back — large images auto-background into a sandbox whose stdout/file-writes never reach disk — stop iterating locally; scaffold a header-only waiver, push, and harvest the exact CVEs from the CI Trivy log (CI is the source of truth). (2) Scan *every* image the security job scans up front — a red image masks staleness in every later image (bit us twice: neo4j→pgvector, pgvector→ollama). (3) Record each waiver in `WAIVERS.md`, not just the scoped file.
- **2026-05-20 — §6.7 exception pre-approved for Issue #4: pin `pgvector:0.8.2` even if <7 days old.** Rationale (user): it's a CVE-*fix* release from a known official publisher; a serious flaw in a ~6-day-old release would most likely already be public, and a still-unknown one is subtle enough that the age-soak wouldn't catch it regardless — so waiting only prolongs exposure to the *known* CVEs the bump fixes. Trivy-cleanliness + the documented waiver remain the real gates. Record the exception in the PR / waiver file when applied. (This is the "no exceptions without explicit conversation" clause being exercised, not removed.)
- **2026-05-21 — Docker image age soak lowered 14 → 7 days (images only; packages stay 14).** Base images come from known signed official publishers and the dominant risk is *known CVEs*, where a fresher rebuild is safer — so Trivy CVE-cleanliness is the primary gate and a 7-day soak still allows a compromised-tag alert to surface. Spec §6.7 amended (with rationale), root `CLAUDE.md` updated, new `/pin-image` skill encodes it. `check_dependency_age.py` untouched (it only scans PyPI/npm, never images).
- **2026-05-21 — neo4j pinned to `5.26.25-community-ubi10` + scoped netty waiver (Issue #2).** UBI-10 base reports 0 OS CVEs vs 14 (incl. 2 CRITICAL gnutls) on Debian `-trixie`; the 3 HIGH netty CVEs Neo4j bundles itself (no base variant fixes them) are waived with per-CVE justification in `infra/trivy/neo4j.trivyignore`, wired to the neo4j Trivy step only. All DoS/parsing-desync, unreachable on a 127.0.0.1 single-user deployment. Drop the waiver when Neo4j bumps netty ≥ 4.1.133.
- **2026-05-21 — Process (retro): created `/pin-image` skill** for the image-pinning ritual (Docker Hub tag/date lookup → 7-day check → **dockerized Trivy** variant scan → base choice / scoped-waiver → apply to compose + ci.yml). Corrects the stale M0 "no trivy in WSL" assumption: `docker run aquasec/trivy image …` works locally and is the verify-before-push path. `add-dependency` gained a one-line "images → use /pin-image" pointer.
- **2026-05-20 — Primary keys are app-generated UUIDs (`uuid4`), not serial integers.** Paragraph/entity IDs are referenced cross-store (Neo4j `source_paragraph_id`, `entity_mentions.paragraph_id`), so store-independent stable IDs avoid sequence coordination between Postgres and Neo4j. DB carries `gen_random_uuid()` as a safety default; the repo inserts the model's id explicitly.
- **2026-05-20 — The document-tree migration is hand-written raw SQL (`op.execute`), not `op.create_table`.** A faithful 1:1 transcription of spec §6.4 — including `vector(768)` — without pulling a pgvector SQLAlchemy type into the dep set just to express one column. `target_metadata` stays `None`; no ORM layer (repo is raw async psycopg, columns map 1:1 to domain fields).
- **2026-05-20 — Repo scope is Create/Read/Delete for now; generic Update deferred.** The realistic update is renumbering `order_index` on reorder, which lands with chunking persistence (Session 4); not added speculatively.
- **2026-05-20 — Recipe for adding an `.env`-backed setting recorded in `backend/CLAUDE.md`** (retro outcome): placeholder in `.env.example` → hand the user an append command → dependent tests stay red until set. Captures the friction this session so Neo4j creds / LLM keys don't re-derive it.
- **2026-05-20 — Integration tests use a dedicated `story_forge_test` DB, fixture-managed in the same Postgres instance.** A pytest session fixture creates it, runs `alembic upgrade head`, yields, then drops it. Chosen over an ephemeral compose service / testcontainers: no new dependency, dev data untouched, deterministic. CI gets a pgvector service container.
- **2026-05-20 — Sibling ordering column is `order_index` (plain integer ordinal).** Avoids `order` (SQL reserved word → forced quoting); same name used end-to-end (DB / Pydantic / JSON), no mapping layer. Integer ordinal renumbered on reorder; fractional/lexical rank deferred as speculative. Spec §6.4 amended (inline note), SQL updated.
- **2026-05-20 — M1 sliced into 6 resumable sessions** (this file's structure). Each session is one-conversation-sized, ends green + committed, and records a resume anchor in the handoff block. Driven by `/wrap-session` (end) and `/resume-session` (start).
- **2026-05-20 — API client generator: `openapi-typescript`** (over `orval`/`hey-api`). Emits TS types + a tiny typed `openapi-fetch` client from the backend's `openapi.json`; we hand-write the TanStack Query hooks in `src/lib/api/`, keeping them plain/commented for an outsider. Chosen for the smallest dependency surface and most legible data layer in a portfolio repo.

## Done in previous sessions — Milestone 3 and earlier

_Reverse-chronological, exactly as moved from `PLAN_SHORT.md`'s Done section._

- **2026-06-17 — Session 31: the M3→M4 roll (docs/governance, no feature code) — M3 closed feature-complete, M4 opened with its first slice decomposed, and a process gap that lets review reports go unactioned was closed.** A between-milestones governance session; all three `docs/CLAUDE.md` §3 roll gates ran. **(1) Architecture re-sync** — `meta-architect:review-architecture` produced `architecture/reports/2026-06-17-architecture-review.md` (first full sweep since edges + the relation lifecycle landed across S4b–S4f). No blockers. Folded the one decision-independent drift on sight (`overview.md`'s as-built block was ~5 sessions stale — it still listed the relation graph-write + the review UI as "planned, not yet built"; rewritten to "M3 feature-complete"). Filed **OQ-20**: S4e/S4f shipped a real relation lifecycle (`staged_relations`: held/committable/written/rejected) in code with **no state-machine note**, while its entity twin has had one since S4a — the structural gap. **(2) Cross-cutting curation M3→M4** — every item hand-walked; the list re-titled; **§3.4 graph story-vs-project scoping graduated from "later" to live M4 work** (M4's multi-story breaks the one-story-per-project assumption the graph route rests on); added two carry-forwards (DM-Rel-5 written-edge re-point, which becomes real with M4's entity↔entity merge; the OQ-20 relation-lifecycle drawing). **(3) M4 first slice** — owner chose **inline highlights** (spec §3.5) over multi-story/§3.4 and properties-edit (foundational, low-risk, high portfolio value; unblocks side-panel + manual annotation). Decomposed step-0 → `architecture/proposals/m4-inline-highlights.md` (register **OPEN**, DM-IH-1..8 / OQ-21). The design's centre of gravity is **DM-IH-1 span resolution**: accepted `entity_mentions` carry **null char offsets** (the LLM path stores an evidence quote; the spaCy span with offsets is discarded at accept), so highlighting is a *where-does-the-entity-sit* problem (render-time string search vs persisting real spans vs hybrid; PL inflection is the headline gap) — a read-only projection that leaves most stations n/a and INV-1/9 untouched. **(4) Retro — closed the report-forcing-function gap (owner-raised):** unlike a decision register (blocks the build) or a CVE waiver (re-reds CI), a `review-architecture` report's findings have no forcing function and can be filed-and-forgotten — it nearly happened this session. Closed with a **producer/consumer pairing**: new **`/resume-session` step 3c** triages the latest report's blocker/risk findings (resolved-or-tracked) the way step 3b scans waivers, paired with **`meta-architect:review-architecture` step 7** now requiring findings be written actionable + mirrored to `open-questions.md`; documented in `architecture/AGENTS.md` (with the clarification that step 3c *reads* a report, it does not *run* the architect — the ADR-0002 ritual-wiring deferral stands). **Deferred (owner):** the now-soaked **python-multipart OSV waiver** couldn't drop on the 06-17 roll day (fix 0.0.31 soaks 06-18; a 13-day-old pin fails the ≥14-day gate) → drop on/after 2026-06-18, before the 06-19 `ignoreUntil`. **Checks:** docs/vault only — backend/frontend code gates are no-ops, no deps changed; the vault writes went through the `meta-architect:*` skills (the vault's only writers). **Lessons:** (a) a milestone-boundary `review-architecture` sweep is what catches an update-in-place note that drifted exactly because nobody re-read it (`overview.md`, 5 sessions stale) — the same doc-freshness-as-a-state-machine pattern from the M2→M3 roll; (b) a report is only as good as the forcing function that makes someone act on it — pairing the producer (write findings actionable) with a consumer ritual step (triage them next resume) is the cheap fix, and "reading the artifact" is categorically different from "running the architect" (so it doesn't breach the ADR-0002 wiring deferral); (c) the owner's "don't report just for reporting" is the right instinct — the next session is explicitly a *resolve-and-decide* session (the report findings + OQ-20 + the DM-IH register), not a build session.

- **2026-06-17 — Session 30: M3.S4f shipped (PR #78) — the relation-review UI, closing M3's feature work (the §3.3 cascade + both human gates are complete).** Built the React "decide on relations" surface test-first, the frontend half of the S4a→S4b cut, mirroring `features/extraction-review/`: two hooks (`useRelations` → `GET …/relations`; `useDecideRelation` → `POST …/relations/{id}/decide`, invalidating the story graph **only on commit** so a new edge appears in the §3.4 viewer while a reject refetches just the queue), a **pure keyboard reducer** (J/K nav, **A=commit / R=reject** — a §8.3 subset, owner-confirmed S30), a `RelationCard` (surface triple `subject — predicate → object` + confidence, **surface-strings-v1**, owner-confirmed — the endpoint resolves entity *ids* but not canonical names) and the `RelationQueue` page (window-bound keyboard, per-card in-flight disabling, 409 surface, a graph-viewer link), plus the route + a "Relations" link in the graph header. **Browser-verified end-to-end** against the real backend (3 seeded committable relations → commit wrote a Neo4j edge visible in the graph, reject wrote nothing, queue drained; seed rows cleaned up after). **Reviews — the layered gate paid off a 4th time (#36/#60/#63/#78):** `/review-pr` (self) passed and even listed "409 surfaces an error" as checked-clean, but the 6-finder **`/code-review` caught a real bug** it missed — `decideMessage` mapped HTTP **409 → "already decided"**, while the decide route actually returns 409 for a *stale/held endpoint* and already-decided is a **200** (`already_decided:true`); worse, the test had *masked* it with a fabricated 409 body the backend never sends. **Fixed** the message semantics + the test, and folded two test-discipline gaps the review flagged (a `useDecideRelation` hook test mirroring `useReviewCandidate`; a graph-viewer `relations-link` href assertion). Verified-real nits left unfolded (mirror-shared with `extraction-review`, so folding here would diverge the two queues, or already tracked — noted in the PR body + cross-cutting): keyboard A/R not gated by in-flight mutation; stale decide banner across navigation; the error-to-string mapper skeleton now n=5. **Checks:** frontend lint/format/build + 136 tests green (+4 this session); PR #78 CI 4/4; squash-merged `8223529`. **Retro (2 changes, owner approved "both homes"):** (a) *"derive an HTTP status code's meaning from the backend route, not a sibling feature's mapping — and a fabricated error-body test fixture validates fiction"* → `frontend/src/lib/api/AGENTS.md` **+** a `/review-pr` §2 mirror; (b) *"manual browser verification: the dev stack is long-running and `.env` is populated — migrate the dev DB first (merged migrations don't auto-apply), bring both servers up, seed fixture rows via SQL against the endpoint's real preconditions"* → `frontend/AGENTS.md`. **Lessons:** (a) a frontend status-code branch carries an *assumed contract* — a mapper copy-adapted from a sibling feature silently inherits the wrong meaning, and a test that fabricates the error body makes the broken mapping pass green; verify each status against the route. (b) a long-running dev environment needs *seeding*, not *scouting* — re-establishing facts already true (stack up, `.env` populated) is friction worth writing down once. (c) the multi-agent `/code-review` caught a self-review miss for the **sixth** consecutive substantive PR — and a recovered service error mid-review didn't damage the repo (verified by a clean-tree + diff-scope sweep), so the read-only finder model is robust to that failure.

- **2026-06-16 — Session 29: M3.S4e shipped (PR #76) — the knowledge graph now has human-gated *edges*, completing §9 M3's "clean graph" for relations.** Built the relation-write backend test-first, the §3.3 5th human action ("decide on relations"). **The path:** extraction already staged each paragraph's relations as surface-form triples, but nothing wrote a Neo4j edge (`create_relation` had zero callers). Now a new `RelationReviewService` (the only edge writer) resolves a staged relation's two surface endpoints to the **committed** entity id of the same-paragraph accepted candidate each names (normalised-exact — DM-Rel-2), and writes the edge under an explicit human `decide` action; held/self-loop/ambiguous endpoints are never committable (DM-Rel-7). A new **`staged_relations` table** (additive migration) gives each relation a `staged|written|rejected` lifecycle + audit (DM-Rel-4); `create_relation` went `CREATE` → **idempotent `MERGE` on `uuid5(subject_id, predicate, object_id)`** so the same fact across paragraphs is one edge and a retried decide never doubles (DM-Rel-6). Two endpoints (`GET …/relations`, `POST …/relations/{id}/decide`) with full `responses=`; OpenAPI + typed client regenerated. **Invariant:** broadened **INV-1** to cover edges (not a new INV-10) + INV-9's second witnessed instance; **ADR 0005**; proposal → `accepted`, OQ-19 struck, INDEX refreshed. **No spec amendment** (§3.3 already lists the action). **Reviews:** `/review-pr` (self) caught a self-loop test that wasn't exercising its branch (fixed + added ambiguity + cross-paragraph-collapse tests) and stale "PROPOSED/OPEN" vault status (reconciled); the 7-finder **`/code-review` caught a real bug** — a *changed* merge target was never persisted on the candidate row, so `committed_entity_id` (reused for relation resolution) resolved a same-paragraph endpoint to the **stale** target → edge to the wrong entity; **fixed** by persisting the committed target on merge-accept (status-last) + a regression test. Other finder candidates were refuted by the passing real-Neo4j tests (the "invalid Cypher `$props.id`" claim — edges write fine) or out of the single-user-local threat model (two-reviewer races). **Checks:** backend ruff/format/mypy/pytest (331 passed + 4 model-skips) green; PR #76 CI 4/4 (backend/frontend/security/ollama-smoke); squash-merged to `main`. **Judgment calls (owner-visible):** dropped `staged_relations.project_id` (story_id scopes every query; a paragraph can have relations with zero candidates, so no clean source); `relation_id` isn't story-scoped in the decide route — kept consistent with the existing candidate routes. **Carried follow-up:** per-mention provenance for triple-deduped edges (post-PoC). **Retro (1 change, owner-approved):** added a **"shared-helper reuse"** bullet to `/review-pr` §1 — when a PR routes an existing shared helper to a new consumer, verify the data the helper reads is maintained correctly for the *new* call site (grounded in this PR's `committed_entity_id`/override-merge bug, which the single self-review missed and `/code-review`'s cross-file tracer caught). *Considered & rejected:* a new rule for the "test green for the wrong reason" lesson (already covered by `/review-pr` §6). **Lessons:** (a) reusing a helper across a new caller (`committed_entity_id`) can *promote* a benign pre-existing imprecision (the unpersisted override-merge target) into a real bug — `/code-review`'s cross-file tracer earned its keep, the **sixth** consecutive substantive PR where the multi-agent pass caught a self-review miss; (b) a "drop a guard's test isn't enough" check — a passing test (`test_self_loop_is_dropped`) was green for the *wrong reason* (ambiguity, not self-loop), the kind of false-confidence only an adversarial re-read catches.

- **2026-06-16 — Session 28: planning/decompose (vault-only, no production code) — the M3 relation-write slice designed and its central decisions made, leaving the build a clean test-first start.** A deliberate pre-code session at the "finish M3 for relations" boundary. The wrap is the only commit. **Lessons:** (a) a step-0 decompose on a branchy "completion" slice earns its keep — the lazy-resolution reframe (re-point dissolves) and the `CREATE`-doubles-edge must-fix would both have surfaced mid-implementation otherwise, the most expensive place to find them; (b) a milestone-boundary decompose wants a fresh vault — the INDEX was stale because the rituals don't run `review-architecture` at resume yet (OQ-3), so the stale "Next steps" had to be caught by hand; (c) the meta-architect skills told the operator to read a template that doesn't exist — a small but every-run friction worth a one-line honesty fix.
- **2026-06-16 — Session 27: M3.S4d shipped — manual handpick (full-stack), completing M3 *entity* dedupe; plus an unplanned security-treadmill detour (3 dep PRs) and a retro skill.** **(1) The feature (PR #70), test-first.** New `GET /stories/{id}/entities?q=` lets the author search **all** of a project's accepted entities and pick **any** as the merge target — the safety net for a true duplicate the cascade + on-accept re-match miss. Project-scoped (resolve story→project, §6.4); ranks `q` in Python with the **same RapidFuzz signal the matcher uses** (a shared `_rank` core that `top_alternatives` now delegates to, behaviour-preserving), so the human's search ≈ the machine's match; **no score floor on purpose** (measured: the diminutives handpick exists to catch score *below* cross-category noise, so reachability wins; the human/INV-1 picks); `q` **never reaches Cypher** (only `project_id` binds — injection-safe by construction); 404 declared, OpenAPI + typed client regenerated. Frontend `EntityPicker` + `useEntitySearch` feed the existing `M`/merge-accept path; the window keyboard scheme already yields to the search input; **last-pick-wins** (picking an alternative clears a handpick — the precedence bug `/code-review` caught, fixed). Promoted `_canonical`→`canonical_for_language` so the route resolves the same project-language name the matcher ranks on. **(2) The security treadmill.** Opening the PR surfaced two reds beyond the known vite #68: a backend **OSV SCA** wave (new advisories vs pinned `starlette`/`python-multipart`) and, after fixing it, an **unmasked** Trivy **neo4j** netty HIGH (CVE-2026-50010 — the sequential-unmask `/review-pr` §8 warns of). Cleared with owner-approved **soaked bumps + fix-first time-boxed waivers**: `starlette` 1.2.0 + `python-multipart` 0.0.30 + `vite` 8.0.16 (all soaked) clear 3-of-4 SCA HIGHs + the vite HIGH; residuals still in soak waived with `ignoreUntil` + reachability (127.0.0.1 single-user, no public TLS) + dated drop-when. Merged as PRs **#72** (SCA + neo4j Trivy) and **#73** (vite); **#68 + #71 closed**. Full local Trivy sweep confirmed pgvector + ollama clean (no further unmask). **(3) Checks:** backend ruff/format/mypy/pytest (306 passed + 4 spaCy skips), frontend lint/format/build/vitest (109) — all green on the merged `main`; feature CI 4/4 after rebase. `/review-pr` + `/code-review` both ran (the latter caught the precedence bug); re-confirmed clean on the final byte-identical code. **Retro (1 new skill + 1 amendment):** the real risk the waivers exposed is a **forgotten waiver** → new **`/triage-advisory`** skill owns the advisory lifecycle incl. the **drop-revisit**, and **`/resume-session` step 3b** adds a date-only waiver-expiry scan so expiring waivers surface at session start (CI `ignoreUntil` re-red as backstop); root `AGENTS.md` points at it. **Lessons:** (a) a *measured* threshold beats a planned one — the score-floor would have re-introduced the exact blind spot the feature exists to fix; only checking real RapidFuzz scores caught it. (b) the SCA/Trivy treadmill reds on a post-gap merge against *unchanged* pins, and fixing one gate unmasks the next — scan all gates/images up front (the `/triage-advisory` discipline). (c) a time-boxed waiver is a deliberate "ignore"; the security hole is forgetting to drop it — so the drop-revisit needs to be a *ritual*, not a memory. (d) `/code-review` caught a self-review miss for the **fifth** consecutive substantive PR.
- **2026-06-15 — Session 26: M3.S4c shipped — on-accept live re-match (intra-batch dedup), backend-only, test-first, squash-merged (PR #67).** Closes the gap Session 25's browser walk surfaced: a first pass against the empty graph stages `Janek` ×3 as three un-mergeable NEW proposals. Now each human **accept** re-runs the **deterministic** matcher (Stage 1 RapidFuzz + Stage 2 cosine — **no LLM**) over the still-pending candidates against the just-accepted entity; a strong match (Stage 1 `>85%` **OR** Stage 2 `cosine >0.85`) flips their staged `proposal` `new → merge` (+ target + provenance/alternatives), so duplicates light up in the queue automatically. New `agents/candidate_rematch.py` (`ReMatchService` reusing `MatchingAgent` stage1/stage2; the match signal is built entirely from the accept's own data — entity id + surface name + the mention vector just written — so it adds **zero extra reads**; Stage-1-only when a vector is absent, mirroring the staging fail-closed gate) + `postgres_candidate_store.update_proposal` (a `status='review-queued'` SQL guard) + an optional `rematch` collaborator on `CandidateReviewService.accept`, called *after* the status flip and **fail-closed** (`contextlib.suppress` — a re-match failure never rolls back the accept; `reject()` and the terminal-noop replay don't fire it). **Monotone** (`new → merge` only, never re-points an existing merge) → idempotent. Writes **only the Postgres `candidates` table** — never Neo4j — so it is the first automated writer of a staged proposal yet **INV-1/INV-9 hold** (the human commits every merge; INV-9's line is graph-vs-staging). Vault folds (witnessed by the flip test): `candidate-lifecycle` gains the `review-queued → review-queued` self-loop; `invariants.md` gets the INV-9 graph-vs-staging clarification; OQ-18 records **ADR 0005 declined**. Tests: re-match unit (flip per stage, no-flip, monotone skip, Stage-1-only, idempotent) + accept-path unit (rematch after status flip, fail-closed, reject/replay don't fire) + the integration **flip test** (accept `Janek` → 2 pending Janeks flip to merge, graph node count unchanged by re-match). **Reviews:** `/review-pr` + multi-agent `/code-review` (high) both ran, **no confirmed defects** — the one candidate ("raw cosine into `confidence`") refuted as matching the existing `candidate_staging` convention and unreachable on the `>0.85` flip path. Full suite **301 passed**; ruff/format/mypy --strict clean. **Merge-readiness:** CI green on backend/security/ollama-smoke; the **frontend `npm audit` job was red on a pre-existing, unrelated vite advisory that also reds `main`** (diagnosed, filed as **Issue #68**) — squash-merged `3326f6a` under the green-main exception, stated in the commit body. **Retro (1 change):** added a "lead with plain language when asking the owner to decide" rule to root `AGENTS.md` (see Decided). **Lessons:** (a) building the match signal from the accept's own data kept re-match a zero-extra-read, fail-closed enhancement — the simplest thing that closed the gap; (b) the green-main exception is exactly for an unrelated dependency-treadmill red like #68 — diagnose + track + state it, don't scope-creep the fix into an unrelated PR; (c) a jargon-dense owner question is friction worth a durable rule, not just an in-the-moment reword.
- **2026-06-15 — Session 25: M3.S4b review-queue UI shipped (PR #65); the milestone's first end-to-end browser run surfaced a real dedup gap → M3.S4c decomposed + spec §3.3 amended.** Two arcs. **(1) M3.S4b — the Stage-4 human gate (frontend), test-first.** `features/extraction-review/`: two generated-client-typed TanStack Query hooks (`useCandidates` queue fetch + `useReviewCandidate` accept/reject mutation — accept invalidates the queue *and* the story-graph key so the graph fills as the author commits; reject invalidates only the queue), a **pure keyboard reducer** (`reviewQueue.ts` — §8.3 J/K nav, A accept, N new, M merge-cycle, R reject) kept out of the components, a presentational `CandidateCard` (quote ±200, NEW-vs-MERGE proposal, reasoning, top-3 alternatives) and the `ReviewQueue` container (states, per-candidate pending, a window keydown listener with an editable-target guard), wired into routing + a graph-viewer link. - **2026-06-15 — Session 24: M3.S4a shipped — intercept-before-write, the cascade's invariant flip, test-first, squash-merged green (PR #63).** The milestone-defining change: extraction stops writing the graph and *stages* each candidate into a new Postgres `candidates` table with the §3.3 cascade's proposal (embed-on-extract → Matching S1/S2 → Judge S3, fail-closed) — **zero** Neo4j nodes; the graph is written **only** by the human-accept endpoints (`GET …/candidates`, `POST …/accept|reject`), the first code enforcer of INV-1. This **retired the temporary INV-8** (no-dedupe `CREATE`-on-extract) and **added INV-9** ("no automated stage writes the graph"); the flip is witnessed by the rewritten coordinator test + an integration test ("extract → 0 nodes, accept → 1 node"), replacing M2.S4's two-identical-→-two-nodes test. `Neo4jRepo.create_entity` became an idempotent **MERGE-on-id** (+ `add_alias` for merge); the accept path writes Neo4j → `entity_mention`(+context vector) → `candidate_decisions` evidence → **status-flip-last**, with deterministic accept-path ids making a crash-before-flip retry idempotent (merge re-validates the target → 409 on TOCTOU). New `candidate_decisions` (INV-3 evidence; the §4.2 `edit_history` text-edit dataset stays deferred) + `paragraph_processed` resume marker (fixes M2's zero-candidate reprocess wart). **ADR 0004** authored; `architecture/invariants.md` / `candidate-lifecycle.md` (→ `living`) / `overview` / `open-questions` / `glossary` / `INDEX` reconciled. **Scope honesty:** relations are *staged* (JSONB) but the edge write + re-point-on-merge is **S4b**; INV-2 consent gate **deferred past M3**; §10 q8 (bilingual peering) surfaced as the spec's deferred call. **Cross-cutting folded:** store-down→**503** (psycopg `OperationalError` + neo4j `ServiceUnavailable`) + a FastAPI lifespan that closes the Neo4j driver. **Reviews — the layered gate paid off again:** `/review-pr` passed but the multi-agent **`/code-review` caught a real fail-closed gap the single pass missed** — `JudgeAgent` propagated the router's transport/envelope errors raw, so a judge outage escaped the cascade's `except JudgeError` and 502'd the whole batch; fixed by making the judge's give-up contract *total* (transport → `JudgeError`). The GitHub Codex secondary was usage-limited (best-effort, not blocked on). **CI surfaced** what review didn't: the `ExtractResponse` field rename (`entities_written`/`relations_written` → `candidates_staged`) left three **frontend test fixtures** on the old shape, red in the frontend `tsc` build — fixed + pushed. **Checks:** 287 backend + 51 frontend tests pass; ruff/format/mypy/tsc clean; CI green 4/4; squash-merged `4c607cf`. **Retro (2 changes):** (a) *"regenerating the typed API client ≠ reconciling its consumers — grep `frontend/src` for the old+new field names on any route-shape change"* → `frontend/src/lib/api/AGENTS.md` + `/review-pr` §2; (b) *"make an agent's give-up error total so a consumer can fail-close on one exception type"* → `backend/src/story_forge/AGENTS.md` (Agents) + `/review-pr` §1. **Lessons:** (a) an API-shape change has *code consumers* (hooks, components, **test fixtures**) that the regenerated client doesn't update — they fail `tsc`, not lint, so they slip a review that only reads the diff; grep them. (b) when one component fail-closes on another's failure, the `except` must cover the error classes that flow *past* the inner component's own give-up error (the router's transport/envelope errors), not just that error — otherwise "provider unavailable" is the one failure that *isn't* fail-closed. (c) the multi-agent `/code-review` caught what `/review-pr` missed for the **third** consecutive substantive PR (#36, #60, #63) — the "run both for substantive code" rule keeps earning its place.
- **2026-06-15 — Session 23: governance-only (no feature code) — M3.S4 re-sliced and the milestone's remaining decisions resolved, ahead of the milestone-closing build.** A deliberate pre-code session at the M3.S4 boundary: the decompose showed the review-queue session is too big for one conversation, so it was split and the open owner decisions settled, leaving the next session a clean test-first start.
